Section 1:
FIRST REPRINT S.B. 495
SENATE BILL NO. 495–COMMITTEE ON
HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES
(ON BEHALF OF THE OFFICE OF THE GOVERNOR)
MAY 15, 2025
____________
Referred to Committee on Health and Human Services
SUMMARY—Revises provisions relating to health care.
(BDR 40-1037)
FISCAL NOTE: Effect on Local Government: May have Fiscal Impact.
Effect on the State: Contains Appropriation included in
Executive Budget.
CONTAINS UNFUNDED MANDATE (§§ 20-22, 72.8)
(NOT REQUESTED BY AFFECTED LOCAL GOVERNMENT)
~
EXPLANATION – Matter in bolded italics is new; matter between brackets [omitted material] is material to be omitted.
AN ACT relating to health care; revising requirements governing
the electronic maintenance, transmittal and exchange of
health information; making revisions relating to
emergency medical care; prescribing certain requirements
to expedite the credentialing and privileging of providers
of health care; authorizing paramedics to serve as
employees or volunteers in hospitals under certain
circumstances; imposing certain requirements governing
prior authorization for medical care and payment of health
insurance claims; making various revisions relating to
Medicaid; creating and prescribing the duties of the
Office of Mental Health in the Department of Health and
Human Services or the Nevada Health Authority, if it is
created; prohibiting noncompetition covenants governing
certain providers of health care; requiring the
prioritization of certain applications for licensure as a
physician or osteopathic physician; requiring certain
providers of health care to provide certain data to the
Department; requiring certain reports of the Board of
Medical Examiners and the State Board of Osteopathic
-
*SB495_R1*
– 2 –
Medicine to include certain information; authorizing the
establishment of an alternative pathway to licensure as a
dental hygienist; establishing provisions to incentivize the
provision of psychological services to rural patients;
requiring the Patient Protection Commission to study
academic medical centers; making appropriations;
providing a penalty; and providing other matters properly
relating thereto.
Legislative Counsel’s Digest:
1 Existing law requires the Department of Health and Human Services, or the
2 Director of the Department or the divisions thereof, to conduct various programs
3 for the improvement of public health and health care in this State. (NRS 433.702-
4 433.744, 439.4921-439.525, 439.529-439.5297, 439.630, 439A.111-439A.185,
5 439A.200-439A.290, 442.710-442.745, 457.230-457.280, 458.025, 458A.090,
6 458A.100, 458A.110)
7 Section 7 of this bill requires the Director to conduct a biennial assessment of
8 the health care workforce needs of this State, which must identify health care
9 professions and specialties, types of clinical services and expertise and geographic
10 areas experiencing critical shortages of providers of health care or clinical services
11 or expertise. Section 42 of this bill provides that such an assessment is not a
12 regulation and is therefore not subject to notice-and-comment rulemaking.
13 Existing law requires the Director to prescribe by regulation a framework for
14 the electronic maintenance, transmittal and exchange of electronic health records,
15 prescriptions, health-related information and electronic signatures and requirements
16 for electronic equivalents of written entries or written approvals. With certain
17 exceptions, existing law requires various entities involved in health care, including
18 persons and facilities that provide health care, to maintain, transmit and exchange
19 health information in accordance with those regulations. (NRS 439.589) Section
20 3.6 of this bill prohibits those regulations from authorizing such a person or entity
21 to comply with that requirement by connecting with a health information exchange
22 or utilizing any other service that charges a fee for providing electronic health
23 records to such a person or entity or a patient upon request. Section 72.8 of this
24 bill: (1) requires a custodian of health care records to furnish electronic health
25 records to a patient or certain other entities upon the request of a patient within 7
26 business days; and (2) prohibits a custodian of health care records from charging a
27 fee to furnish health care records under such circumstances.
28 Sections 3.3, 72.3 and 126 of this bill limit the health care providers that must
29 maintain, transmit and exchange health information electronically to medical
30 facilities and high-level providers of health care. Section 1 of this bill defines the
31 term “high-level provider of health care” to mean a physician, physician assistant,
32 dentist, advanced practice registered nurse, chiropractic physician, podiatric
33 physician or physical therapist. Section 3.3 additionally exempts from requirements
34 to maintain, transmit and exchange health information electronically high-level
35 providers of health care whose solo or group practices are under a certain size.
36 However, section 3.3 requires such high-level providers of health care to furnish
37 the medical records of a patient electronically to the patient or another person or
38 entity upon request of the patient. Section 4.5 of this bill makes conforming
39 changes to revise the applicability of a provision requiring the Department to notify
40 the licensing board of a provider who fails to comply with requirements governing
41 the electronic maintenance, transmittal and exchange of health information. Section
42 1.5 of this bill establishes the applicability of the definition set forth in section 1,
43 and sections 43, 45.5, 67.9, 116.3 and 116.7 of this bill make other conforming
-
*SB495_R1*
– 3 –
44 changes to indicate the proper placement of section 1 in the Nevada Revised
45 Statutes. Section 72.5 of this bill updates internal references changed by
46 section 72.3.
47 Existing law prohibits a person or entity from operating an independent center
48 for emergency medical care without a license issued by the Division of Public and
49 Behavioral Health of the Department. (NRS 449.030) Section 22.5 of this bill
50 requires a facility that is structurally separate from the hospital and provides
51 services for the treatment of a medical emergency, including such a facility that is
52 owned or operated by, or otherwise part of, a hospital, to be licensed as an
53 independent center for emergency medical care. (NRS 449.0151, 449.030) Sections
54 24.3 and 24.5 of this bill prohibit the Division or the State Board of Health from
55 charging a fee for the issuance of such a license. Section 24.8 of this bill prohibits
56 the Division from issuing a license to operate an independent center for emergency
57 medical care that is located within a 5 mile radius of another independent center for
58 emergency medical care or a hospital with an emergency department. However,
59 section 120.6 of this bill requires the Division to issue a license to certain such
60 independent centers for emergency medical care that are currently licensed or had
61 taken certain steps toward operating by January 1, 2025. Section 26.5 of this bill
62 requires an independent center for emergency medical care to provide urgent care
63 services during all operating hours and imposes certain additional requirements
64 related to the provision of such urgent care, except that section 120.3 of this bill
65 exempts from that requirement independent centers for emergency medical care
66 that are licensed on the date on which this bill is enacted.
67 Existing law establishes programs to increase awareness of information
68 concerning hospitals and surgical centers for ambulatory patients. (NRS 439A.200-
69 439A.290) Section 9.5 of this bill requires the Department to establish a similar
70 program to increase awareness of information concerning independent centers for
71 emergency medical care. Sections 9.5, 10.5, 12.5, 13.5 and 27.3 of this bill provide
72 for the Department to collect certain information on the operations of independent
73 centers for emergency medical care and the outcomes for patients treated by
74 independent centers for emergency medical care. To facilitate such reporting,
75 section 27.3 requires an independent center for emergency medical care to use the
76 same form prescribed by the Director for discharging patients as a hospital is
77 currently required to use. Section 95.5 of this bill makes a conforming change to
78 reflect that independent centers for emergency medical care will be using the same
79 form. Sections 12.5 and 13.5 require the Department to: (1) make certain
80 information concerning independent centers for emergency medical care available
81 upon request; and (2) post certain information concerning independent centers for
82 emergency medical care on an Internet website maintained by the Department.
83 Sections 11.2 and 41.5 of this bill make conforming changes to add references to
84 independent centers for emergency medical care to sections that discuss the
85 program and associated website. Section 8.5 of this bill defines the term
86 “independent center for emergency medical care” for that purpose. Section 11.5 of
87 this bill establishes the applicability of certain definitions. Section 27.7 of this bill
88 requires a report prepared by the Director on the status of the programs to increase
89 public awareness of information concerning hospitals and surgical centers for
90 ambulatory patients to additionally include information on the status of the program
91 to increase awareness of information concerning independent centers for
92 emergency medical care. Section 51.3 of this bill requires the Director of the
93 Department, to the extent that money is available, to include under Medicaid a
94 system of value-based payments for care provided by independent centers for
95 emergency medical care to recipients of Medicaid.
96 Existing law authorizes a court, upon a petition, to order the sealing of records
97 of certain convictions if the person who was convicted: (1) has not been convicted
98 of any additional offense, except for minor traffic violations, for a specified period
-
*SB495_R1*
– 4 –
99 of time; and (2) does not have charges pending for any offense, except for minor
100 traffic violations. (NRS 179.245) Existing law also authorizes a court, upon a
101 petition, to order the sealing of records of an arrest where the charges were
102 dismissed, the prosecutor declined to prosecute or the person who was arrested was
103 acquitted. (NRS 179.255) Section 32.5 of this bill authorizes the Department or the
104 Division of Health Care Financing and Policy of the Department to review certain
105 sealed records for the purpose of determining the suitability of the person to whom
106 the records pertain to serve as a provider of services under Medicaid or to own or
107 serve as an officer, managing employee or managing agent of such a provider of
108 services.
109 Existing law prescribes a procedure for conducting a hearing to review an
110 action taken against a provider of services under Medicaid. (NRS 422.306) Section
111 51.5 of this bill requires such a provider of services to maintain and provide certain
112 documents to the Department for the purpose of verifying claims. Section 51.5
113 authorizes the Department to deny a claim or recover money already paid if the
114 Department is unable to verify the claim. Section 51.8 of this bill: (1) prescribes a
115 process for the Department to review claims for appropriateness and propriety; and
116 (2) authorizes the Department to deny or recover any amount paid pursuant to such
117 a claim or take certain actions based on such a review. Section 119.5 of this bill
118 makes an appropriation to the Division of Health Care Financing and Policy of the
119 Department and authorizes the expenditure of certain other money to carry out
120 sections 51.3-51.8.
121 Section 67 of this bill: (1) creates the Office of Mental Health within the
122 Department; and (2) requires the Director to appoint the Executive Director of the
123 Office. Section 67.2 of this bill requires the Office to perform certain duties to
124 improve access to and the effectiveness of mental health services in this State.
125 Section 67.4 of this bill requires the Office to perform certain additional duties
126 related to the mental and behavioral health of children. Sections 67.6-67.8 of this
127 bill require the subcommittee on the mental health of children of the Commission
128 on Behavioral Health and each mental health consortium to support those duties.
129 Section 67.5 of this bill requires the Office to submit a biennial report to the
130 Legislature. Section 66.6 of this bill defines the term “Office” for the purposes of
131 sections 67-67.5 to refer to the Office of Mental Health. Senate Bill No. 494 of this
132 legislative session proposes to create a new department in the Executive Branch of
133 State Government known as the Nevada Health Authority to perform certain duties
134 related to health care, including behavioral health care, in this State. Section 121.5
135 of this bill transfers the Office to the Nevada Health Authority if Senate Bill No.
136 494 is enacted.
137 Section 89 of this bill requires the Board of Psychological Examiners to: (1)
138 take certain actions to incentivize licensees to receive continuing education
139 concerning the mental health needs of patients in rural areas; and (2) establish a
140 program to recognize psychologists who provide at least 200 hours of services
141 through telehealth to such patients.
142 Sections 20, 46, 50, 75, 85, 109 and 113 of this bill prescribe requirements to
143 expedite the process of credentialing providers of health care to participate in
144 public and private health insurance plans. Beginning on January 1, 2027, sections
145 117 and 118 of this bill require insurers that issue such plans, or entities to which
146 such insurers delegate credentialing functions, to process least 95 percent of
147 complete requests for such credentialing not later than 60 days after receiving all of
148 the information necessary to complete such a request. Beginning on January 1,
149 2027, section 21 of this bill similarly requires a hospital to process at least 95
150 percent of complete requests from providers of health care for privileges to perform
151 services at the hospital not later than 60 days after receiving all of the information
152 necessary to complete such a request.
-
*SB495_R1*
– 5 –
153 Existing law authorizes an emergency medical technician, advanced emergency
154 medical technician or paramedic who holds the proper endorsement to provide
155 services, known as community paramedicine services, to patients who do not
156 require emergency medical transportation. (NRS 450B.1993) Sections 29-31 of this
157 bill authorize paramedics to serve as employees or volunteers in a hospital under
158 certain circumstances and with certain limitations.
159 Existing law provides that a noncompetition covenant is void unless the
160 covenant: (1) is supported by valuable consideration; (2) does not impose any
161 restraint that is greater than is required for the protection of the employer; (3) does
162 not impose any undue hardship on the employee; and (4) imposes restrictions that
163 are appropriately related to the consideration for the covenant. (NRS 613.195)
164 Section 71 of this bill provides that a noncompetition covenant may not apply to a
165 provider of health care whose primary duties involve providing clinical care to
166 patients and who is not employed or contracted to primarily perform administrative
167 tasks.
168 Sections 74 and 84 of this bill require the Board of Medical Examiners and the
169 State Board of Osteopathic Medicine, respectively, to establish by regulation a
170 procedure for prioritizing applications for licensure as a physician or osteopathic
171 physician of applicants who plan to: (1) serve underserved geographic areas or
172 populations in this State; or (2) practice a specialty for which there is a shortage in
173 this State. Sections 76 and 86 of this bill require certain reports submitted by those
174 Boards to the Governor and Legislature to include information relating to the
175 efficiency of the process for licensing physicians or osteopathic physicians, as
176 applicable.
177 Existing law requires the Director to: (1) develop and make available to each
178 professional licensing board that licenses, certifies or registers providers of health
179 care an electronic data request that solicits certain information relating to the
180 demographics and practices of providers of health care; and (2) establish and
181 maintain a database of information collected through the data request. (NRS
182 439A.116) Under existing law, providers of health care applying to renew a license,
183 certificate or registration may, but are not required to, complete the data request.
184 (NRS 450B.805, 630.2671, 630A.327, 631.332, 632.3423, 633.4716, 634.1303,
185 634A.169, 635.111, 636.262, 637.145, 637B.192, 639.183, 640.152, 640A.185,
186 640B.405, 640D.135, 640E.225, 641.2215, 641A.217, 641B.281, 641C.455,
187 652.126) Sections 76.5, 82.3, 82.6, 86.2-86.8 and 89.2-89.9 of this bill make
188 completion of the data request mandatory to renew a license, certificate or
189 registration issued by: (1) the Board of Medical Examiners; (2) the Board of Dental
190 Examiners of Nevada; (3) the State Board of Nursing; (4) the State Board of
191 Osteopathic Medicine; (5) the State Board of Podiatry; (6) the Nevada State Board
192 of Optometry; (7) the Board of Dispensing Opticians; (8) the Board of
193 Psychological Examiners; (9) the Board of Examiners for Marriage and Family
194 Therapists and Clinical Professional Counselors; (10) the Board of Examiners for
195 Social Workers; (11) the Board of Examiners for Alcohol, Drug and Gambling
196 Counselors; and (12) the Board of Applied Behavior Analysis. Section 42.5 of this
197 bill makes a conforming change to ensure the confidentiality of information
198 submitted through such a data request.
199 Existing law requires an applicant for licensure as a dental hygienist to have
200 graduated from an accredited program of dental hygiene that meets certain
201 requirements. (NRS 631.290) Sections 77 and 79 of this bill authorize the Board of
202 Dental Examiners of Nevada to establish by regulation an alternative training
203 pathway involving a course of training under the supervision of a licensed dentist
204 that an applicant for such a license may complete instead of graduating from such a
205 program. Section 77 requires an applicant who has completed the alternative
206 training pathway to have also successfully passed: (1) a competency examination
207 conducted by the supervising dentist; (2) a written examination; and (3) a clinical
-
*SB495_R1*
– 6 –
208 examination approved by the Board. Section 78 of this bill requires such an
209 applicant to submit with his or her application for licensure proof that he or she has
210 passed those examinations. Section 77 provides that a person who completes the
211 alternative training pathway is only eligible for licensure if he or she began the
212 pathway during a biennium during which there was shortage of dental hygienists, as
213 documented by the assessment conducted pursuant to section 7. Section 77
214 requires the Board to adopt regulations establishing the scope of practice of a dental
215 hygienist who has completed the alternative training pathway. Section 81 of this
216 bill prohibits a dental hygienist who has completed the alternative training pathway
217 and has not subsequently graduated from an accredited program of dental hygiene
218 from prescribing and dispensing preventive agents.
219 Existing law requires the Department to administer Medicaid and the
220 Children’s Health Insurance Program. (NRS 422.270) Existing federal law
221 authorizes: (1) a hospital to elect to make determinations concerning whether
222 certain persons are presumptively eligible for Medicaid; and (2) a state to allow
223 certain other entities to make such determinations. (42 U.S.C. §§ 1396a(a)(47),
224 1396r-1, 1396r-1a, 1396r-1b, 1396r-1c) Section 51 of this bill requires the
225 Department to take certain measures to facilitate such presumptive eligibility
226 determinations by the personnel of hospitals and qualified community-based
227 organizations. Section 51 also requires the Department to audit such entities to
228 ensure that the presumptive eligibility determinations made by the personnel of
229 those entities are accurate and comply with applicable law.
230 Existing law authorizes certain health insurers to require prior authorization
231 before an insured may receive coverage for medical and dental care in certain
232 circumstances. If an insurer requires prior authorization, existing law requires the
233 insurer to: (1) file its procedure for obtaining prior authorization with the
234 Commissioner of Insurance for approval; and (2) respond to a request for prior
235 authorization within 20 days after receiving the request. (NRS 687B.225)
236 Beginning on January 1, 2028, sections 47, 53-62, 69, 97-108 and 110 of this bill
237 establish additional requirements relating to the use of prior authorization for
238 medical care by health insurers, including Medicaid, the Children’s Health
239 Insurance Program and insurance for state employees, as well as certain entities
240 with which such insurers contract to perform functions relating to prior
241 authorization. Sections 53.5, 54, 55 and 98-100 define certain terms, and sections
242 53 and 97 establish the applicability of those definitions. Section 101.6 of this bill
243 requires certain insurers and other entities that employ or utilize an artificial
244 intelligence system or automated decision tool to process requests for prior
245 authorization to transmit a notice to each insured that: (1) discloses the insurer’s use
246 of the system or tool to process requests for prior authorization; and (2) describes
247 certain aspects of the system or tool. Sections 56 and 110 require an insurer or
248 other entity that performs functions relating to prior authorization to respond to a
249 request for prior authorization within a specified period of time. If an insurer or
250 other entity that performs functions relating to prior authorization is unable to
251 approve or deny a request for prior authorization within that time period, sections
252 56 and 110 require the insurer or entity to notify the insured and his or her provider
253 of health care of the delay. Sections 58 and 102 prescribe the required contents of
254 that notice. Sections 59 and 103 require an insurer or other entity that performs
255 functions relating to prior authorization to provide similar notice upon denying a
256 request for prior authorization and establish a process to appeal such a denial.
257 Sections 56 and 110 prohibit insurers and other entities that perform functions
258 relating to prior authorization from requiring prior authorization for covered
259 emergency services. Sections 57 and 101 require insurers and other entities that
260 perform functions relating to prior authorization to implement an electronic system
261 for receiving and processing requests for prior authorization. Sections 22 and 72 of
-
*SB495_R1*
– 7 –
262 this bill require certain medical facilities and providers of health care to submit
263 requests for prior authorization through those systems.
264 Sections 60 and 104 limit the circumstances under which an insurer or other
265 entity that performs functions relating to prior authorization may: (1) revoke the
266 approval of a request for prior authorization; (2) delay or deny payment for care to
267 which such a request pertains; or (3) assign a lower billing code or otherwise
268 reduce the payment for such care. Sections 61 and 105 prescribe certain
269 requirements to ensure the continuity of care for an insured whose benefits are
270 terminated or who switches health insurance plans. Sections 62 and 106 provide
271 for the reporting and publication of certain information relating to prior
272 authorization and the payment of claims. Section 107 establishes the Gold Card
273 Exemption Program to exempt providers of health care whose requests for prior
274 authorization are approved at a rate of at least 95 percent from the requirement to
275 obtain prior authorization for certain services. Section 56 requires the Department,
276 with respect to Medicaid and the Children’s Health Insurance Program, or a
277 Medicaid managed care organization to grant Gold Card Exemptions to providers
278 of health care in accordance with section 107 except in certain circumstances.
279 Section 63 of this bill requires Medicaid and the Children’s Health Insurance
280 Program to comply with certain requirements governing the prompt payment of
281 claims that apply under existing law to private insurers and the Public Employees’
282 Benefits Program. (NRS 683A.0879, 689A.410, 689B.255, 689C.355, 689A.188,
283 695B.2505, 695C.185, 695D.215) Section 63 additionally requires Medicaid to
284 comply with certain federal requirements governing the timely payment of claims
285 under Medicaid. (42 C.F.R. § 447.45(d)(2),(3))
286 Section 108 requires the Commissioner to adopt regulations prescribing: (1)
287 requirements to ensure that applicants for certain certificates or approval to engage
288 in business related to insurance are equipped to comply with certain requirements
289 governing prior authorization and the payment of health claims; and (2) criteria to
290 ensure that an insurer or other entity that enters into a contract to provide services
291 for certain public insurance programs is in compliance with those requirements.
292 Sections 45, 91, 93-95 and 116 of this bill make various changes to establish the
293 applicability of those regulations. Section 92 of this bill makes a conforming
294 change to indicate the proper placement of section 91 in the Nevada Revised
295 Statutes. Section 108 additionally requires the Commissioner to perform certain
296 other duties relating to the implementation and enforcement of requirements
297 governing prior authorization and the payment of health claims. Section 65 of this
298 bill requires the prior authorization policies and procedures for prescription drugs
299 under Medicaid to comply with sections 53-63. Section 41 of this bill requires the
300 Director of the Department to administer sections 50-63 in the same manner as
301 other provisions governing Medicaid. Sections 47, 69 and 114 of this bill make
302 sections 97-108 and 110 applicable to insurance for state and private employees
303 and nonprofit hospital or medical services corporations. Section 101.3 of this bill
304 makes sections 101.8-105 and 110 inapplicable to Medicaid managed care
305 organizations, which are instead required to comply with sections 56 and 58-61.
306 Sections 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 90, 111 and 112 of this bill make conforming changes
307 concerning the applicability and enforcement of sections 20-22 and 109.
308 Section 121 of this bill requires the Patient Protection Commission to conduct a
309 study during the 2025-2026 interim concerning academic medical centers in this
310 State, and section 120 of this bill appropriates money for the study.

– 8 –
THE PEOPLE OF THE STATE OF NEVADA, REPRESENTED IN
SENATE AND ASSEMBLY, DO ENACT AS FOLLOWS:
1 Section 1. Chapter 439 of NRS is hereby amended by adding
2 thereto a new section to read as follows:
3 “High-level provider of health care” means a physician or
4 physician assistant licensed pursuant to chapter 630 or 633 of
5 NRS, dentist, advanced practice registered nurse, chiropractic
6 physician, podiatric physician or physical therapist.
7 Sec. 1.5. NRS 439.581 is hereby amended to read as follows:
8 439.581 As used in NRS 439.581 to 439.597, inclusive, and
9 section 1 of this act, unless the context otherwise requires, the
10 words and terms defined in NRS 439.582 to 439.585, inclusive, and
11 section 1 of this act have the meanings ascribed to them in those
12 sections.
13 Sec. 2. (Deleted by amendment.)
14 Sec. 2.5. NRS 439.588 is hereby amended to read as follows:
15 439.588 1. A health information exchange shall not operate
16 in this State without first obtaining certification as provided in
17 subsection 2.
18 2. The Director shall by regulation establish the manner in
19 which a health information exchange may apply for certification and
20 the requirements for granting such certification, which must include,
21 without limitation, that the health information exchange demonstrate
22 its financial and operational sustainability, adherence to the privacy,
23 security and patient consent standards adopted pursuant to NRS
24 439.589 and capacity for interoperability with any other health
25 information exchange certified pursuant to this section.
26 3. The Director may deny an application for certification or
27 may suspend or revoke any certification issued pursuant to
28 subsection 2 for failure to comply with the provisions of NRS
29 439.581 to 439.597, inclusive, and section 1 of this act or the
30 regulations adopted pursuant thereto or any applicable federal or
31 state law.
32 4. When the Director intends to deny, suspend or revoke a
33 certification, he or she shall give reasonable notice to all parties by
34 certified mail. The notice must contain the legal authority,
35 jurisdiction and reasons for the action to be taken. A health
36 information exchange that wishes to contest the action of the
37 Director must file an appeal with the Director.
38 5. The Director shall adopt regulations establishing the manner
39 in which a person may file a complaint with the Director regarding a
40 violation of the provisions of this section.
41 6. The Director may impose an administrative fine against a
42 health information exchange which operates in this State without
-
*SB495_R1*
– 9 –
1 holding a certification in an amount established by the Director by
2 regulation. The Director shall afford a health information exchange
3 so fined an opportunity for a hearing pursuant to the provisions of
4 NRS 233B.121.
5 7. The Director may adopt such regulations as he or she
6 determines are necessary to carry out the provisions of this section.
7 Sec. 3. (Deleted by amendment.)
8 Sec. 3.3. NRS 439.589 is hereby amended to read as follows:
9 439.589 1. The Director, in consultation with health care
10 providers, third parties and other interested persons and entities,
11 shall by regulation prescribe a framework for the electronic
12 maintenance, transmittal and exchange of electronic health records,
13 prescriptions, health-related information and electronic signatures
14 and requirements for electronic equivalents of written entries or
15 written approvals in accordance with federal law. The regulations
16 must:
17 (a) Establish standards for networks and technologies to be used
18 to maintain, transmit and exchange health information, including,
19 without limitation, standards:
20 (1) That require:
21 (I) The use of networks and technologies that allow
22 patients to access electronic health records directly from the health
23 care provider of the patient and forward such electronic health
24 records electronically to other persons and entities; and
25 (II) The interoperability of such networks and
26 technologies in accordance with the applicable standards for the
27 interoperability of Qualified Health Information Networks
28 prescribed by the Office of the National Coordinator for Health
29 Information Technology of the United States Department of Health
30 and Human Services;
31 (2) To ensure that electronic health records retained or shared
32 are secure;
33 (3) To maintain the confidentiality of electronic health
34 records and health-related information, including, without
35 limitation, standards to maintain the confidentiality of electronic
36 health records relating to a child who has received health care
37 services without the consent of a parent or guardian and which
38 ensure that a child’s right to access such health care services is not
39 impaired;
40 (4) To ensure the privacy of individually identifiable health
41 information, including, without limitation, standards to ensure the
42 privacy of information relating to a child who has received health
43 care services without the consent of a parent or guardian;
44 (5) For obtaining consent from a patient before retrieving the
45 patient’s health records from a health information exchange,
-
*SB495_R1*
– 10 –
1 including, without limitation, standards for obtaining such consent
2 from a child who has received health care services without the
3 consent of a parent or guardian;
4 (6) For making any necessary corrections to information or
5 records;
6 (7) For notifying a patient if the confidentiality of
7 information contained in an electronic health record of the patient is
8 breached;
9 (8) Governing the ownership, management and use of
10 electronic health records, health-related information and related
11 data; and
12 (9) For the electronic transmission of prior authorizations for
13 prescription medication;
14 (b) Ensure compliance with the requirements, specifications and
15 protocols for exchanging, securing and disclosing electronic health
16 records, health-related information and related data prescribed
17 pursuant to the provisions of the Health Information Technology for
18 Economic and Clinical Health Act, 42 U.S.C. §§ 300jj et seq. and
19 17901 et seq., the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability
20 Act of 1996, Public Law 104-191, and other applicable federal and
21 state law; and
22 (c) Be based on nationally recognized best practices for
23 maintaining, transmitting and exchanging health information
24 electronically.
25 2. The standards prescribed pursuant to this section must
26 include, without limitation:
27 (a) Requirements for the creation, maintenance and transmittal
28 of electronic health records;
29 (b) Requirements for protecting confidentiality, including
30 control over, access to and the collection, organization and
31 maintenance of electronic health records, health-related information
32 and individually identifiable health information;
33 (c) Requirements for the manner in which a patient may,
34 through a health care provider who participates in the sharing of
35 health records using a health information exchange, revoke his or
36 her consent for a health care provider to retrieve the patient’s health
37 records from the health information exchange;
38 (d) A secure and traceable electronic audit system for
39 identifying access points and trails to electronic health records and

29 Sec. 7. 1. On or before July 1 of each even-numbered year,
30 the Department, in collaboration with the Health Care Workforce
31 Working Group established pursuant to NRS 439A.118, shall:
32 (a) Conduct a comprehensive assessment of needs with regard
33 to the health care workforce in this State; and
34 (b) Compile a report of the results of the assessment and
35 submit the report to the Governor and the Director of the
36 Legislative Counsel Bureau for transmittal to the Joint Interim
37 Standing Committee on Health and Human Services and the next
38 regular session of the Legislature.
39 2. The assessment conducted pursuant to paragraph (a) of
40 subsection 1 must consist of:
41 (a) A quantitative analysis of the health care workforce in this
42 State, including, without limitation:
43 (1) A determination of the total number of providers of
44 health care in this State and the total number of providers of
-
*SB495_R1*
– 17 –
1 health care in this State who practice different professions and
2 different specialties within those professions;
3 (2) A determination of the total number of providers of
4 health care who practice in different geographic areas of this State
5 and the total number of providers of health care who practice
6 different professions and different specialties within those
7 geographic areas; and
8 (3) A comparison of the numbers of providers of health
9 care identified pursuant to subparagraphs (1) and (2) with
10 benchmarks established by the Health Resources and Services
11 Administration of the United States Department of Health and
12 Human Services or nationally recognized organizations that
13 prescribe such benchmarks;
14 (b) A determination of the most critical shortages in the health
15 care workforce of this State, prioritizing:
16 (1) Essential health care professions and specialties and
17 essential clinical services or expertise currently experiencing
18 shortages; and
19 (2) Geographic areas of this State that are experiencing the
20 most critical shortages of providers of health care or clinical
21 services or expertise;
22 (c) An identification of unmet needs for specific health
23 technology and therapies, including, without limitation, genomic
24 testing, clinical trials, cellular therapies and palliative care; and
25 (d) A determination of any areas where there is an oversupply
26 of providers of health care, including, without limitation,
27 specialists or clinical services.
28 3. The report compiled pursuant to paragraph (b) of
29 subsection 1 must include, without limitation:
30 (a) A summary of the assessment conducted pursuant to
31 paragraph (a) of subsection 1, including, without limitation:
32 (1) An analysis of shortages of providers of health care,
33 shortages of clinical services or expertise and unmet health needs
34 in this State; and
35 (2) A description of shortages of providers of health care
36 and the shortages of clinical services or expertise by geographic
37 region, including rural and urban areas; and
38 (b) Recommendations for legislation and regulatory changes
39 to improve the recruitment and retention of providers of health
40 care.

*SB495_R1*

6 439A.020 The purposes of this chapter are to:
7 1. Promote equal access to quality health care at a reasonable

12 care;

22 decisions;

3 2. The Department shall:
4 (a) Publicize the availability of the Internet website;
5 (b) Update the information contained on the Internet website at
6 least quarterly;
7 (c) Ensure that the information contained on the Internet website
8 is accurate and reliable;
9 (d) Ensure that the information reported by a hospital , [or]
10 surgical center for ambulatory patients or independent center for
11 emergency medical care for inpatients and outpatients which is
12 contained on the Internet website is expressed as a total number and
13 as a rate, and [must be] is reported in a manner so as not to reveal
14 the identity of a specific inpatient or outpatient of a hospital , [or]
15 surgical center for ambulatory patients [;] or independent center for
16 emergency medical care;
17 (e) Post a disclaimer on the Internet website indicating that the
18 information contained on the website is provided to assist with the
19 comparison of hospitals and independent centers for emergency
20 medical care and is not a guarantee by the Department or its
21 employees as to the charges imposed by the hospitals and
22 independent centers for emergency medical care in this State or the
23 quality of the services provided by the hospitals and independent
24 centers for emergency medical care in this State, including, without
25 limitation, an explanation that the actual amount charged to a person
26 by a particular hospital or independent center for emergency
27 medical care may not be the same charge as posted on the website
28 for that hospital [;] or independent center for emergency medical
29 care.
30 (f) Provide on the Internet website established pursuant to this
31 section a link to the Internet website of the Centers for Medicare and
32 Medicaid Services of the United States Department of Health and
33 Human Services; and
34 (g) Upon request, make the information that is contained on the
35 Internet website available in printed form.
36 3. As used in this section, “diagnosis-related group” means
37 groupings of medical diagnostic categories used as a basis for

39 care plans.

1 Sec. 19. Chapter 449 of NRS is hereby amended by adding
2 thereto the provisions set forth as sections 20, 21 and 22 of this act.
3 Sec. 20. 1. A medical facility to which a third party
4 delegates credentialing functions shall comply with the provisions
5 of section 50 or 109 of this act, where applicable.
6 2. As used in this section:
7 (a) “Credentialing” means verifying the credentials of a
8 provider of health care for the purpose of determining whether the
9 provider of health care meets the requirements for participation in
10 the network of a third party or participation in Medicaid or the
11 Children’s Health Insurance Program as a provider of services.
12 (b) “Network” has the meaning ascribed to it in
13 NRS 687B.640.
14 (c) “Provider of health care” has the meaning ascribed to it in
15 NRS 629.031.
16 (d) “Third party”:
17 (1) Except as otherwise provided in subparagraph (2),
18 means any insurer or organization providing health coverage or
19 benefits in accordance with state or federal law.
20 (2) Does not include:
21 (I) A plan that is subject to the Employee Retirement
22 Income Security Act of 1974 or any information relating to such
23 coverage; or
24 (II) Health coverage provided by a local government
25 agency through a self-insurance reserve fund pursuant to
26 NRS 287.010.
27 Sec. 21. 1. A hospital shall, for at least 95 percent of the
28 complete requests for privileging submitted by providers of health
29 care to the hospital, process the request not later than 60 days
30 after the hospital receives all information necessary to complete
31 the request.
32 2. Not later than 15 days after a hospital receives an
33 incomplete request for privileging from a provider of health care,
34 the hospital shall notify the provider of health care of the
35 information necessary to complete the request.
36 3. A hospital shall immediately notify the Division of:
37 (a) Any delay in privileging that exceeds the time period
38 specified in subsection 1;
39 (b) Steps taken to ensure that the request that is subject to the
40 delay is processed as quickly as possible; and
41 (c) An anticipated timeline to complete the processing of the
42 request.
43 4. On or before February 1 of each year, a hospital shall
44 compile and submit to the Division a report on the privileging of
45 providers of health care which includes, without limitation:
-
*SB495_R1*
– 26 –
1 (a) The average time between the submission by a provider of
2 health care of a request for privileging and the request being
3 approved or denied;
4 (b) The rates at which the hospital processes requests for
5 privileging within the time period specified in subsection 1; and
6 (c) Any planned improvements to the hospital’s process for
7 privileging providers of health care, including, without limitation,
8 improvements to technology or procedures to increase the
9 efficiency of the process.
10 5. As used in this section, “privileging” means the process of
11 determining whether to authorize a provider of health care to
12 provide specific services at a hospital based on his or her
13 credentials and qualifications.
14 Sec. 22. 1. A hospital or surgical center for ambulatory
15 patients shall submit requests for prior authorization to third
16 parties using the electronic systems implemented pursuant to
17 sections 57 and 101 of this act, where applicable.
18 2. As used in this section, “third party”:
19 (a) Except as otherwise provided in paragraph (b), means any
20 insurer or organization providing health coverage or benefits in
21 accordance with state or federal law.
22 (b) Does not include:
23 (1) A plan that is subject to the Employee Retirement
24 Income Security Act of 1974 or any information relating to such
25 coverage; or
26 (2) Health coverage provided by a local government agency
27 through a self-insurance reserve fund pursuant to NRS 287.010.

33 Sec. 26.5. NRS 449.1818 is hereby amended to read as
34 follows:
35 449.1818 1. Each off-campus location of a hospital shall
36 obtain and use and include on all claims for reimbursement or
37 payment for health care services provided at the location a national
38 provider identifier that is distinct from the national provider
39 identifier used by the main campus and any other off-campus
40 location of the hospital. If the off-campus location includes the
41 national provider identifier on such a claim, the off-campus location
42 may also include on the claim the national provider identifier used
43 by the main campus of the hospital. If the off-campus location
44 includes both the national provider identifier used by the off-campus
45 location and the national provider identifier used by the main
-
*SB495_R1*
– 32 –
1 campus on a claim, the claim must clearly identify which national
2 provider identifier corresponds to the off-campus location and
3 which national provider identifier corresponds to the main campus.
4 2. An independent center for emergency medical care shall
5 include on all claims for reimbursement or payment for health care
6 services provided at the independent center for emergency medical
7 care the national provider identifier used by the independent center
8 for emergency medical care.
9 3. An independent center for emergency medical care:
10 (a) Shall provide urgent care during all operating hours
11 through:
12 (1) A separate urgent care unit within the independent
13 center for emergency medical care; or
14 (2) A system that uses the severity of the patient’s condition
15 to determine whether the patient receives emergency services or
16 urgent care;
17 (b) Shall not charge more for urgent care than the amount
18 customarily charged for urgent care by an urgent care center;
19 (c) If urgent care services are sufficient to treat or manage the
20 condition of a patient, shall inform the patient that he or she may
21 receive urgent care rather than emergency services; and
22 (d) Shall not require a patient to wait longer to receive urgent
23 care services than a patient with the same condition would be
24 required to wait to receive emergency services.
25 4. As used in this section:
26 (a) “National provider identifier” means the standard, unique
27 health identifier for health care providers that is issued by the
28 national provider system in accordance with 45 C.F.R. Part 162.
29 (b) “Off-campus location” means a facility:
30 (1) With operations that are directly or indirectly owned or
31 controlled by, in whole or in part, a hospital or which is affiliated
32 with a hospital, regardless of whether it is operated by the same
33 governing body as the hospital;
34 (2) That is located more than 250 yards from the main
35 campus of the hospital;
36 (3) That provides services which are organizationally and
37 functionally integrated with the hospital; and
38 (4) That is an outpatient facility providing ambulatory
39 surgery, urgent care or emergency room services.
40 (c) “Urgent care” means health care that is furnished to a
41 person whose medical condition is sufficiently acute to require
42 treatment unavailable through, or inappropriate to be provided by,
43 a clinic or the office of a provider of health care, but not so acute
44 as to require treatment in an emergency room.

42 Sec. 28. Chapter 450B of NRS is hereby amended by adding

44 Sec. 29. 1. The State Board of Health shall adopt
45 regulations authorizing paramedics to be employed by or volunteer
-
*SB495_R1*
– 35 –
1 in hospitals, including, without limitation, emergency
2 departments, intensive care units and other areas for acute or
3 specialty care.
4 2. The regulations adopted pursuant to this section must:
5 (a) Ensure that paramedics who are employed by or volunteer
6 in hospitals perform their duties in a manner that enhances the
7 care of patients while maintaining the safety of patients;
8 (b) Prescribe the duties and responsibilities of a paramedic
9 who is employed by or volunteering in a hospital, which must vary
10 depending on the training and experience of the paramedic;
11 (c) Prescribe standards of training for a paramedic who is
12 employed by or volunteering in a hospital, including, without
13 limitation:
14 (1) Any certifications that such a paramedic must hold; and
15 (2) Any additional training required for paramedics who
16 work in specialty areas or provide care to patient with severe
17 conditions or urgent needs; and
18 (d) Establish specific protocols for the oversight and periodic
19 evaluation of paramedics who are employed by or are volunteering
20 in hospitals in a manner that ensures compliance with the
21 regulations adopted pursuant to this section and the policies
22 developed pursuant to section 30 of this act.
23 Sec. 30. 1. A hospital that employs paramedics or accepts
24 paramedics as volunteers pursuant to section 29 of this act must
25 develop and implement comprehensive written policies that:
26 (a) Define the scope of duties of such paramedics within the
27 hospital in accordance with the regulations adopted pursuant to

30 paramedics within the hospital in accordance with the regulations
31 adopted pursuant to section 29 of this act, including, without
32 limitation, procedures for:
33 (1) The delegation of tasks to such paramedics by
34 physicians, nurses and other qualified providers of health care;
35 and
36 (2) The review by providers of health care described in
37 subparagraph (1) of tasks performed by such paramedics;
38 (c) Ensure compliance with applicable standards for
39 accreditation and the safety of patients and state and federal law
40 and regulations, including, without limitation, procedures for
41 internal reviews and audits of the duties of such paramedics to
42 ensure adherence to such standards, laws and regulations; and
43 (d) Establish protocols to document the outcomes of patients
44 who receive services from such paramedics.

4 233B.038 1. “Regulation” means:
5 (a) An agency rule, standard, directive or statement of general

7 describes the organization, procedure or practice requirements of
8 any agency;
9 (b) A proposed regulation;
10 (c) The amendment or repeal of a prior regulation; and
11 (d) The general application by an agency of a written policy,
12 interpretation, process or procedure to determine whether a person is
13 in compliance with a federal or state statute or regulation in order to
14 assess a fine, monetary penalty or monetary interest.

18 public;
19 (b) A declaratory ruling;

14 711.600, and section 89.9 of this act, sections 35, 38 and 41 of
15 chapter 478, Statutes of Nevada 2011 and section 2 of chapter 391,
16 Statutes of Nevada 2013 and unless otherwise declared by law to be
17 confidential, all public books and public records of a governmental
18 entity must be open at all times during office hours to inspection by
19 any person, and may be fully copied or an abstract or memorandum
20 may be prepared from those public books and public records. Any
21 such copies, abstracts or memoranda may be used to supply the
22 general public with copies, abstracts or memoranda of the records or
23 may be used in any other way to the advantage of the governmental
24 entity or of the general public. This section does not supersede or in
25 any manner affect the federal laws governing copyrights or enlarge,
26 diminish or affect in any other manner the rights of a person in any
27 written book or record which is copyrighted pursuant to federal law.
28 2. A governmental entity may not reject a book or record
29 which is copyrighted solely because it is copyrighted.
30 3. A governmental entity that has legal custody or control of a
31 public book or record shall not deny a request made pursuant to
32 subsection 1 to inspect or copy or receive a copy of a public book or
33 record on the basis that the requested public book or record contains
34 information that is confidential if the governmental entity can
35 redact, delete, conceal or separate, including, without limitation,
36 electronically, the confidential information from the information
37 included in the public book or record that is not otherwise
38 confidential.
39 4. If requested, a governmental entity shall provide a copy of a
40 public record in an electronic format by means of an electronic
41 medium. Nothing in this subsection requires a governmental entity
42 to provide a copy of a public record in an electronic format or by
43 means of an electronic medium if:
44 (a) The public record:
45 (1) Was not created or prepared in an electronic format; and
-
*SB495_R1*
– 46 –
1 (2) Is not available in an electronic format; or
2 (b) Providing the public record in an electronic format or by
3 means of an electronic medium would:
4 (1) Give access to proprietary software; or
5 (2) Require the production of information that is confidential
6 and that cannot be redacted, deleted, concealed or separated from
7 information that is not otherwise confidential.
8 5. An officer, employee or agent of a governmental entity who
9 has legal custody or control of a public record:
10 (a) Shall not refuse to provide a copy of that public record in the
11 medium that is requested because the officer, employee or agent has
12 already prepared or would prefer to provide the copy in a different
13 medium.
14 (b) Except as otherwise provided in NRS 239.030, shall, upon
15 request, prepare the copy of the public record and shall not require

31 Sec. 51.8. 1. If the Department determines that a provider
32 of services under Medicaid may be prescribing or providing

34 Medicaid, is unnecessary or otherwise conflicts with applicable
35 professional standards or the requirements of the Medicaid
36 program, the Department shall perform a review of the relevant
37 claims to evaluate the appropriateness and propriety of the
38 services for which payment is claimed. If the Department has not
39 paid the claims, the review must occur before the Department pays
40 the claims.

42 1, the Department shall:
43 (a) Notify the provider of services who submitted the claims
44 subject to the review; and
-
*SB495_R1*
– 53 –
1 (b) Require the provider of services to submit to the
2 Department within a period of time specified by the Department
3 any documentation necessary to substantiate the claims.
4 3. If a provider of services fails to submit the documentation
5 required by the Department pursuant to paragraph (b) of
6 subsection 2 within the time specified pursuant to that paragraph,
7 the Department may take the actions described in paragraph (a) of
8 subsection 5 without the opportunity for a hearing pursuant to
9 NRS 422.306.
10 4. Not later than 60 days after receiving the documentation
11 requested pursuant to paragraph (b) of subsection 2, the
12 Department shall complete a review pursuant to this section and
13 either:
14 (a) Pay the claims that were subject to the review or, if the
15 Department has already paid such a claim, notify the provider of
16 services who made the claim that the claim has been upheld; or
17 (b) Take an action described in paragraph (a) of subsection 5
18 with respect to the claims that were subject to the review.

22 recipients of Medicaid, is unnecessary or otherwise conflicts with
23 applicable professional standards or the requirements of the
24 Medicaid program, the Department may, after the opportunity for
25 a hearing pursuant to NRS 422.306:
26 (a) Deny the affected claims or, if the Department has already

28 the provider;
29 (b) Require the provider to request and receive authorization

32 (c) Take any other action authorized by this chapter and the

26 (4) Instructions, written in clear language that is
27 understandable to an ordinary layperson, describing how the
28 recipient can appeal the denial through the process established
29 pursuant to subsection 2; and
30 (5) A description of any documentation that may be
31 necessary or pertinent to an appeal.
32 (b) The provider of health care who submitted the request or
33 the person designated by the provider of health care to manage
34 requests for prior authorization an electronic notice that includes
35 all the information required by the Rules described in subsection 1
36 of section 56 of this act.
37 2. The Department or a Medicaid managed care entity shall
38 establish a process that allows a recipient to appeal the denial of a
39 request for prior authorization. The process must allow for the
40 clear resolution of each appeal within a reasonable time.
41 Sec. 60. 1. The Department or a Medicaid managed care
42 entity, with respect to Medicaid and the Children’s Health
43 Insurance Program, shall not revoke a request for prior
44 authorization that the Department or Medicaid managed care
45 entity, as applicable, has previously approved or delay or deny
-
*SB495_R1*
– 59 –
1 payment for the medical or dental care to which such a request
2 pertains unless the Department or Medicaid managed care entity,
3 as applicable, determines that:
4 (a) A recipient or a provider of health care procured the
5 approval by fraud or material misrepresentation;
6 (b) The approval was affected by a clerical error; or
7 (c) The person to which the medical or dental care was
8 provided was not, on the date on which the care was provided, a
9 recipient.
10 2. After approving a request for prior authorization, the
11 Department or a Medicaid managed care entity shall not assign a
12 lower level billing code to the medical or dental care to which the
13 request pertains or otherwise reduce the payment for such care
14 below the amount indicated in the request for prior authorization
15 without a clear, documented justification that aligns with
16 applicable standards of care.
17 3. If the Department or a Medicaid managed care entity takes
18 any action described in subsection 1 or 2, the Department or
19 Medicaid managed care entity shall provide written notice of the
20 action using the same remittance process that the Department or
21 Medicaid managed care entity, as applicable, uses to pay claims to
22 the provider of health care that submitted the request for prior
23 authorization. Such notice must include, without limitation, a
24 detailed description of the justification for the action and
25 documentation supporting that justification.
26 4. As used in this section, “clerical error” means a
27 typographical or administrative error or an error in calculation.
28 The term does not include any mistake relating to clinical
29 judgment, the medical necessity of care or the appropriateness of a
30 treatment.
31 Sec. 61. 1. The Department or a Medicaid managed care

*SB495_R1*

12 4. If the Department or a Medicaid managed care entity

21 Sec. 63. 1. The Department shall comply with the
22 requirements of 42 C.F.R. § 447.45(d)(2) and (3).
23 2. If the Department approves a claim under Medicaid or the
24 Children’s Health Insurance Program, the Department shall pay
25 the claim within 30 days after it is approved. Except as otherwise
26 provided in this section, if the approved claim is not paid within
27 that period, the Department shall pay interest on the claim at a
28 rate of interest equal to the prime rate at the largest bank in
29 Nevada, as ascertained by the Commissioner of Financial
30 Institutions, on January 1 or July 1, as the case may be,
31 immediately preceding the date on which the payment was due,
32 plus 6 percent. The interest must be calculated from 30 days after
33 the date on which the claim is approved until the date on which
34 the claim is paid.
35 3. If the Department requires additional information to
36 determine whether to approve or deny a claim under Medicaid or
37 the Children’s Health Insurance Program, it shall notify the
38 claimant of its request for the additional information within 20
39 days after it receives the claim. The Department shall notify the
40 provider of health care of all the specific reasons for the delay in
41 approving or denying the claim. The Department shall approve or
42 deny the claim within 30 days after receiving the additional
43 information. If the claim is approved, the insurer shall pay the
44 claim within 30 days after it receives the additional information. If
45 the approved claim is not paid within that period, the Department
-
*SB495_R1*
– 62 –
1 shall pay interest on the claim in the manner prescribed in
2 subsection 2.
3 4. The Department shall not request a claimant to resubmit
4 information that the claimant has already provided to the
5 Department, unless the Department provides a legitimate reason
6 for the request and the purpose of the request is not to delay the
7 payment of the claim, harass the claimant or discourage the filing
8 of claims.
9 5. The Department shall not pay only part of a claim that has
10 been approved and is fully payable.
11 6. If the failure to pay an approved claim within the time
12 period specified in subsection 2 or 3 is the fault of an entity with
13 which the Department has contracted to perform functions
14 relating to the payment of claims under Medicaid or the
15 Children’s Health Insurance Program, the Department may
16 collect from that person reimbursement for the cost of the interest
17 required by those subsections.

39 Sec. 67. 1. The Office of Mental Health is hereby created
40 within the Department.
41 2. The Governor shall appoint the Executive Director of the
42 Office. The Executive Director:
43 (a) Serves at the pleasure of the Governor;
44 (b) Shall serve as the executive head of the Office; and
-
*SB495_R1*
– 64 –
1 (c) Must have relevant professional experience in the field of

3 candidates who have:

5 (2) Designing and administering systems of care, including,
6 without limitation, community-based care, for persons with
7 behavioral health needs.

9 interest in the performance of his or her duties. Such prohibited
10 conflicts of interest include, without limitation:
11 (a) A financial interest or other personal interest in any entity
12 that:
13 (1) Provides behavioral health services; or
14 (2) Owns, operates or controls an entity that provides
15 behavioral health services.
16 (b) Currently receiving payment from any person or entity
17 other than the Department for the provision of behavioral health
18 services.

20 donations from any source for the purpose of carrying out the

22 5. As used in this section, “behavioral health services”
23 includes, without limitation, treatment or other services for
24 persons with mental illnesses or persons with substance use
25 disorders.
26 Sec. 67.2. The Office shall perform such activities and

3 433B.335 1. Each mental health consortium established

11 2. In preparing the long-term strategic plan pursuant to
12 subsection 1, each mental health consortium must be guided by the
13 following principles:
14 (a) The system of mental health services set forth in the plan
15 should be centered on children with emotional disturbance and their
16 families, with the needs and strengths of those children and their
17 families dictating the types and mix of services provided.
18 (b) The families of children with emotional disturbance,
19 including, without limitation, foster parents, should be active
20 participants in all aspects of planning, selecting and delivering
21 mental health services at the local level.
22 (c) The system of mental health services should be community-
23 based and flexible, with accountability and the focus of the services
24 at the local level.
25 (d) The system of mental health services should provide timely
26 access to a comprehensive array of cost-effective mental health
27 services.
28 (e) Children and their families who are in need of mental health
29 services should be identified as early as possible through screening,
30 assessment processes, treatment and systems of support.
31 (f) Comprehensive mental health services should be made
32 available in the least restrictive but clinically appropriate
33 environment.
34 (g) The family of a child with an emotional disturbance should
35 be eligible to receive mental health services from the system.
36 (h) Mental health services should be provided to children with
37 emotional disturbance in a sensitive manner that is responsive to
38 cultural and gender-based differences and the special needs of the
39 children.

27 Sec. 71. NRS 613.195 is hereby amended to read as follows:
28 613.195 1. A noncompetition covenant is void and
29 unenforceable unless the noncompetition covenant:
30 (a) Is supported by valuable consideration;
31 (b) Does not impose any restraint that is greater than is required
32 for the protection of the employer for whose benefit the restraint is
33 imposed;
34 (c) Does not impose any undue hardship on the employee; and
35 (d) Imposes restrictions that are appropriate in relation to the
36 valuable consideration supporting the noncompetition covenant.
37 2. A noncompetition covenant may not restrict, and an
38 employer may not bring an action to restrict, a former employee of
39 an employer from providing service to a former customer or client
40 if:
41 (a) The former employee did not solicit the former customer or
42 client;
43 (b) The customer or client voluntarily chose to leave and seek
44 services from the former employee; and
-
*SB495_R1*
– 71 –
1 (c) The former employee is otherwise complying with the
2 limitations in the covenant as to time, geographical area and scope
3 of activity to be restrained, other than any limitation on providing
4 services to a former customer or client who seeks the services of the
5 former employee without any contact instigated by the former
6 employee.
7  Any provision in a noncompetition covenant which violates the
8 provisions of this subsection is void and unenforceable.
9 3. A noncompetition covenant may not apply to [an] :
10 (a) An employee who is paid solely on an hourly wage basis,
11 exclusive of any tips or gratuities [.] ; or
12 (b) A patient-facing provider of health care.
13 4. An employer in this State who negotiates, executes or
14 attempts to enforce a noncompetition covenant that is void and
15 unenforceable under this section does not violate the provisions of
16 NRS 613.200.
17 5. If the termination of the employment of an employee is the
18 result of a reduction of force, reorganization or similar restructuring
19 of the employer, a noncompetition covenant is only enforceable
20 during the period in which the employer is paying the employee’s
21 salary, benefits or equivalent compensation, including, without
22 limitation, severance pay.
23 6. If an employer brings an action to enforce a noncompetition
24 covenant or an employee brings an action to challenge a
25 noncompetition covenant and the court finds the covenant is
26 supported by valuable consideration but contains limitations as to
27 time, geographical area or scope of activity to be restrained that are
28 not reasonable, imposes a greater restraint than is necessary for the
29 protection of the employer for whose benefit the restraint is imposed
30 or imposes undue hardship on the employee, the court shall revise
31 the covenant to the extent necessary and enforce the covenant as
32 revised. Such revisions must cause the limitations contained in the
33 covenant as to time, geographical area and scope of activity to be
34 restrained to be reasonable, to not impose undue hardship on the
35 employee and to impose a restraint that is not greater than is

21 Sec. 84. 1. The Board shall adopt regulations establishing
22 a procedure to prioritize the processing of applications for the
23 initial issuance of a license to practice osteopathic medicine
24 submitted by an applicant who intends to practice:
25 (a) Serving geographic areas and populations of this State
26 where the shortage of providers of health care is most critical, as
27 identified by the assessment conducted pursuant to section 7 of
28 this act; or
29 (b) In a specialty for which the need is most critical, as
30 identified by the assessment conducted pursuant to section 7 of
31 this act.

33 adopted pursuant to this section, the Board shall:

35 applications described in subsection 1 to ensure compliance with
36 the requirements of that subsection; and

38 Human Services, annually update the geographic areas,
39 populations and specialties for which applications are prioritized

41 this act.

1 paragraph (b) of subsection 1 of section 109 of this act, as

9 assistant to indicate whether he or she wishes to allow electronic

13 provider of health care for the purpose of determining whether the
14 provider of health care meets the requirements for participation in
15 the network of a third party or participation in Medicaid or the
16 Children’s Health Insurance Program as a provider of services.
17 (b) “Network” has the meaning ascribed to it in
18 NRS 687B.640.

20 authorize a provider of health care to provide specific services at a
21 hospital based on his or her credentials and qualifications.
22 (d) “Provider of health care” has the meaning ascribed to it in
23 NRS 629.031.

25 (1) Except as otherwise provided in subparagraph (2),

5 Sec. 99. “Insured” means a policyholder, subscriber,
6 enrollee or other person covered by a health carrier.
7 Sec. 100. “Provider of health care” has the meaning
8 ascribed to it in NRS 695G.070.
9 Sec. 101. 1. Each health carrier in this State shall
10 implement an electronic system for receiving and processing
11 requests for prior authorization. Such a system must:
12 (a) Allow providers of health care to electronically submit,
13 track and receive updates concerning requests for prior
14 authorization; and
15 (b) Comply with:
16 (1) The Connectivity Rules, Eligibility and Benefits
17 Operating Rules and Health Care Claims Operating Rules
18 prescribed by the Committee on Operating Rules for Information
19 Exchange of the Council for Affordable Quality Healthcare, or its
20 successor organization;
21 (2) The provisions of the Prior Authorization and Referrals
22 Operating Rules prescribed by the Committee on Operating Rules
23 for Information Exchange of the Council for Affordable Quality
24 Healthcare, or its successor organization, which relate to prior
25 authorization; and
26 (3) Where applicable, any federal laws or regulations
27 governing electronic systems for receiving and processing requests
28 for prior authorization applicable to Medicare Advantage plans
29 and health care plans to provide health care services to recipients
30 of Medicaid or insurance pursuant to the Children’s Health
31 Insurance Program.
32 2. The Commissioner, in collaboration with the Department
33 of Health and Human Services, shall review each revision to the
34 Rules described in subparagraphs (1) and (2) of paragraph (b) of
35 subsection 1 to ensure their suitability for this State. If the
36 Commissioner determines that a revision is not suitable for this
37 State, the Commissioner shall hold a public hearing within 6
38 months after the date the Rules were revised to review his or her
39 determination. If the Commissioner does not revise his or her
40 determination, the Commissioner shall give notice within 30 days
41 after the hearing that the revisions are not suitable for this State.
42 3. If the Commissioner does not give notice pursuant to
43 subsection 2 that a revision to the Rules described in

45 suitable for this State within the time period prescribed in
-

2 pursuant to subsection 1 must comply with the revision not later

4 4. The Commissioner shall annually publish a report on an

7 of this section.
8 5. As used in this section, “Medicare Advantage plan” means

21 Sec. 101.3. The provisions of NRS 687B.225 and sections
22 101.6 to 105, inclusive, of this act, do not apply to:

30 such services.

32 performs any function related to prior authorization for an entity
33 described in subsection 1, while the administrator or utilization
34 review organization, as applicable, is performing such functions.
35 Sec. 101.6. 1. If a health carrier utilizes an artificial
36 intelligence system or automated decision tool to process requests
37 for prior authorization, the health carrier shall make available, in
38 a place that is readily accessible and conspicuous to insureds and
39 the public:
40 (a) A statement that the health carrier utilizes an artificial
41 intelligence system or automated decision tool to process requests
42 for prior authorization;
43 (b) A general description of how the artificial intelligence
44 system or automated decision tool works; and
-
*SB495_R1*
– 99 –
1 (c) A description of the specific types of information or data
2 utilized by the artificial intelligence system or automated decision
3 tool to generate an outcome.
4 2. As used in this section:
5 (a) “Artificial intelligence system” means a machine-based
6 system that can, for a given set of human-defined objectives, make
7 predictions, recommendations or decisions influencing real or
8 virtual environments.
9 (b) “Automated decision tool” means an automated or
10 computerized system that is specifically developed or modified to
11 make, or be a controlling factor in making, consequential
12 decisions.
13 Sec. 102. Upon determining that it is necessary to delay
14 approving or denying a request for prior authorization beyond the
15 period prescribed by paragraph (b) of subsection 2 or subsection 3
16 or 4, as applicable, of NRS 687B.225, a health carrier shall
17 transmit a written notice to the insured to whom the request
18 pertains and an electronic notice to the provider of health care
19 who submitted the request or the person designated by the provider
20 of health care to manage requests for prior authorization. Such
21 notice must contain:
22 1. A specific description of all reasons that the health carrier
23 is delaying the response;
24 2. The steps necessary to resolve the delay; and
25 3. The anticipated timeline for resolving the delay.
26 Sec. 103. 1. Upon denying a request for prior
27 authorization, a health carrier shall transmit to:
28 (a) The insured to whom the request pertains a written notice
29 that contains:
30 (1) A specific description of all reasons that the health
31 carrier denied the request;
32 (2) A description of any documentation that the health
33 carrier requested from the insured or a provider of health care of
34 the insured and did not receive or deemed insufficient, if the
35 failure to receive sufficient documentation contributed to the
36 denial;
37 (3) A statement that the insured has the right to appeal the
38 denial;
39 (4) Instructions, written in clear language that is
40 understandable to an ordinary layperson, describing how the
41 insured can appeal the denial through the process established
42 pursuant to subsection 2; and
43 (5) A description of any documentation that may be
44 necessary or pertinent to an appeal.
-
*SB495_R1*
– 100 –
1 (b) The provider of health care who submitted the request or
2 the person designated by the provider of health care to manage
3 requests for prior authorization an electronic notice that includes
4 all the information required by the Rules described in paragraph
5 (b) of subsection 2 of NRS 687B.225.
6 2. A health carrier shall establish a process that allows an
7 insured to appeal the denial of a request for prior authorization.
8 The process must allow for the clear resolution of each appeal
9 within a reasonable time.
10 Sec. 104. 1. A health carrier shall not revoke a request for
11 prior authorization that the health carrier has previously approved
12 or delay or deny payment for the medical care to which such a
13 request pertains unless the health carrier determines that:
14 (a) An insured or a provider of health care procured the
15 approval by fraud or material misrepresentation;
16 (b) The approval was affected by a clerical error; or
17 (c) The person to which the medical care was provided was
18 not, on the date on which the care was provided, an insured of the
19 health carrier.
20 2. After a health carrier approves a request for prior
21 authorization, the health carrier shall not assign a lower level
22 billing code to the medical care to which the request pertains or
23 otherwise reduce the payment for such care below the amount
24 indicated in the request for prior authorization without a clear,
25 documented justification that aligns with applicable standards of
26 care.
27 3. A health carrier that takes any action described in
28 subsection 1 or 2 shall provide written notice of the action using
29 the same remittance process that the health carrier uses to pay
30 claims to the provider of health care that submitted the request for
31 prior authorization. Such notice must include, without limitation,
32 a detailed description of the justification for the action and
33 documentation supporting that justification.
34 4. As used in this section, “clerical error” means a
35 typographical or administrative error or an error in calculation.
36 The term does not include any mistake relating to clinical
37 judgment, the medical necessity of care or the appropriateness of a
38 treatment.
39 Sec. 105. 1. A health carrier shall comply with the
40 provisions of 26 U.S.C. § 9818 and 42 U.S.C. § 300gg-113, and
41 any regulations adopted pursuant thereto.
42 2. Within the first 90 days of the coverage period for an
43 insured, a health carrier shall honor a request for prior
44 authorization that has been approved by a health carrier or other
45 entity that previously provided the insured with coverage for
-
*SB495_R1*
– 101 –
1 medical care if the specific medical care included within the
2 request is not affirmatively excluded under the terms and
3 conditions of the contract or policy of insurance issued by the
4 health carrier.
5 3. The health carrier may, within the 90-day period
6 established by subsection 2, undertake an independent review of
7 the medical care that was approved by the health carrier or other
8 entity that previously provided the insured with coverage. The
9 health carrier shall not deny approval in violation of subsection 2
10 as the result of such a review.
11 4. A change in the health carrier’s procedure for obtaining
12 prior authorization or a new exclusion or limitation of coverage
13 adopted by a health carrier may not take effect until the next
14 coverage period with respect to:
15 (a) An insured for whom the health carrier has, within the
16 current coverage period, approved a request for prior
17 authorization; and
18 (b) The medical care that is identical to the care for which the
19 health carrier had previously approved a request for prior
20 authorization within the current coverage period.
21 5. If an insured for whom a request for prior authorization
22 has been approved by a health carrier obtains coverage under a
23 different policy or contract of health insurance issued by the same
24 health carrier, the health carrier shall honor the approval to the
25 same extent as if the insured were still covered under the policy or
26 contract of health insurance under which the insured was covered
27 when the health carrier approved the request.
28 6. As used in this section, “coverage period” means the
29 current term of a contract or policy of insurance issued by a
30 health carrier.
