13 Sec. 102. Upon determining that it is necessary to delay
14 approving or denying a request for prior authorization beyond the
15 period prescribed by paragraph (b) of subsection 2 or subsection 3
16 or 4, as applicable, of NRS 687B.225, a health carrier shall
17 transmit a written notice to the insured to whom the request
18 pertains and an electronic notice to the provider of health care
19 who submitted the request or the person designated by the provider
20 of health care to manage requests for prior authorization. Such
21 notice must contain:
22 1. A specific description of all reasons that the health carrier
23 is delaying the response;
24 2. The steps necessary to resolve the delay; and
25 3. The anticipated timeline for resolving the delay.
26 Sec. 103. 1. Upon denying a request for prior
27 authorization, a health carrier shall transmit to:
28 (a) The insured to whom the request pertains a written notice
29 that contains:
30 (1) A specific description of all reasons that the health
31 carrier denied the request;
32 (2) A description of any documentation that the health
33 carrier requested from the insured or a provider of health care of
34 the insured and did not receive or deemed insufficient, if the
35 failure to receive sufficient documentation contributed to the
36 denial;
37 (3) A statement that the insured has the right to appeal the
38 denial;
39 (4) Instructions, written in clear language that is
40 understandable to an ordinary layperson, describing how the
41 insured can appeal the denial through the process established
42 pursuant to subsection 2; and
43 (5) A description of any documentation that may be
44 necessary or pertinent to an appeal.
-
*SB495_R1*

– 100 –
1 (b) The provider of health care who submitted the request or
2 the person designated by the provider of health care to manage
3 requests for prior authorization an electronic notice that includes
4 all the information required by the Rules described in paragraph
5 (b) of subsection 2 of NRS 687B.225.
6 2. A health carrier shall establish a process that allows an
7 insured to appeal the denial of a request for prior authorization.
8 The process must allow for the clear resolution of each appeal
9 within a reasonable time.
10 Sec. 104. 1. A health carrier shall not revoke a request for
11 prior authorization that the health carrier has previously approved
12 or delay or deny payment for the medical care to which such a
13 request pertains unless the health carrier determines that:
14 (a) An insured or a provider of health care procured the
15 approval by fraud or material misrepresentation;
16 (b) The approval was affected by a clerical error; or
17 (c) The person to which the medical care was provided was
18 not, on the date on which the care was provided, an insured of the
19 health carrier.
20 2. After a health carrier approves a request for prior
21 authorization, the health carrier shall not assign a lower level
22 billing code to the medical care to which the request pertains or
23 otherwise reduce the payment for such care below the amount
24 indicated in the request for prior authorization without a clear,
25 documented justification that aligns with applicable standards of
26 care.
27 3. A health carrier that takes any action described in
28 subsection 1 or 2 shall provide written notice of the action using
29 the same remittance process that the health carrier uses to pay
30 claims to the provider of health care that submitted the request for
31 prior authorization. Such notice must include, without limitation,
32 a detailed description of the justification for the action and
33 documentation supporting that justification.
34 4. As used in this section, “clerical error” means a
35 typographical or administrative error or an error in calculation.
36 The term does not include any mistake relating to clinical
37 judgment, the medical necessity of care or the appropriateness of a
38 treatment.
39 Sec. 105. 1. A health carrier shall comply with the
40 provisions of 26 U.S.C. § 9818 and 42 U.S.C. § 300gg-113, and
41 any regulations adopted pursuant thereto.
42 2. Within the first 90 days of the coverage period for an

42 (b) The provider of health care meets any other requirements

– 104 –
1 (a) Annually review the continued eligibility of a provider of
2 health care who has been granted a Gold Card Exemption
3 pursuant to this section for that Gold Card Exemption; and
4 (b) If the health carrier determines through a review
5 conducted pursuant to paragraph (a) that a provider of health care
6 who holds a Gold Card Exemption no longer meets the
7 requirements of subsection 2:
8 (1) Notify the provider of health care that he or she:
9 (I) Does not meet the requirements to continue to hold a
10 Gold Card Exemption; and
11 (II) May appeal the determination of the health carrier
12 in accordance with the regulations adopted pursuant to subsection
13 8; and
14 (2) Unless the determination that the provider no longer
15 meets the requirements of subsection 2 is reversed on appeal,
16 revoke the Gold Card Exemption.
17 4. Except as otherwise provided in subsections 6, 7 and 8 of
18 section 56 of this act, a health carrier shall not require a provider
19 of health care who holds a Gold Card Exemption to obtain prior
20 authorization for any goods and services to which the Gold Card
21 Exemption applies.
22 5. A health carrier shall maintain on an Internet website
23 maintained by the health carrier a list of all providers of health
24 care who hold a Gold Card Exemption. The list must include, for
25 each provider, the specialty of the provider and the goods and
26 services covered by the Gold Card Exemption.

28 hold Gold Card Exemptions to determine whether those providers

30 regulations adopted thereto. If a health carrier determines that
31 such a provider of health care does not meet those requirements,
32 the health carrier may, after notice and the opportunity for an
33 appeal:
34 (a) Suspend or revoke the Gold Card Exemption; or
35 (b) Impose any other penalties authorized by the regulations
36 adopted pursuant to subsection 8.

27 information necessary to complete the request; and
28 (b) Immediately notify the Commissioner of:
29 (1) Any delay in credentialing that exceeds the time
30 period specified in paragraph (a);
31 (2) Steps taken to ensure that the request that is
32 subject to the delay is processed as quickly as possible; and
33 (3) An anticipated timeline to complete the
34 processing of the request.
35 3. For the purposes of subsection 2, a request for
36 credentialing shall be deemed to be complete if:
37 (a) The provider of health care who submitted the
38 request has completed all fields prescribed by the Council
39 for Affordable Quality Healthcare, or its successor
40 organization;
41 (b) The provider of health care receives electronic notice
42 that the credentialing application is complete; and
43 (c) The completed request is made available through the
44 Portal or successor system described in paragraph (a) of
-
*SB495_R1*

– 116 –
1 subsection 1 to the health carrier or the entity to which the
2 health carrier delegates credentialing functions.
3 4. An entity to which a health carrier delegates
4 credentialing functions shall immediately notify the health
5 carrier of any delay in credentialing that exceeds the time
6 period specified in paragraph (a) of subsection 2. Such
7 notice must include the information listed in paragraph (b)
8 of subsection 2.
9 5. The Commissioner shall:
10 (a) Perform an annual audit of each health carrier that
11 operates in this State to ensure compliance with the
12 requirements of this section;
13 (b) Collect from health carriers and entities to which
14 health carriers designate credentialing functions such data as
15 is necessary to compile the report required by paragraph (b);
16 and
17 (c) On or before February 1 of each year:
18 (1) Compile a report on the credentialing of providers
19 of health care which includes, without limitation:
20 (I) The average time between the submission by a
21 provider of health care of a request to a health carrier for
22 credentialing and the request being approved or denied, for
23 each health carrier in this State and aggregated for all health
24 carriers in this State; [and]
25 (II) The rates at which requests for credentialing
26 are processed within the time period specified in paragraph
27 (a) of subsection 2, for each health carrier in this State and
28 aggregated for all health carriers in this State; and
29 (III) Recommendations for improvements to the
30 process for credentialing providers of health care, including,
31 without limitation, recommendations concerning
32 improvements to technology or procedures to increase the
33 efficiency of the process; and
34 (2) Submit the report to the Governor and the Director
35 of the Legislative Counsel Bureau for transmittal to:
36 (I) In even-numbered years, the Joint Interim
37 Standing Committee on Health and Human Services; and
38 (II) In odd-numbered years, the next regular
39 session of the Legislature.

41 (a) “Credentialing” means verifying the credentials of a

38 Sec. 121. 1. During the 2025-2026 interim, the Patient
39 Protection Commission shall study the adequacy of the academic
40 medical centers in this State. The study must include, without
41 limitation:
42 (a) An assessment of the current and projected health care
43 workforce in this State;
-
*SB495_R1*

– 119 –
1 (b) An evaluation of potential locations for the development or
2 enhancement of academic medical centers in this State, which must
3 consider, without limitation:
4 (1) Equity among the geographic areas of this State; and
5 (2) The needs of the population in the diverse geographic
6 areas of this State for the services of an academic medical center;
7 (c) An analysis of models for sustainable funding of academic
8 medical centers that utilize money from the State and Federal
9 Governments and private persons and entities;
10 (d) Recommendations for integrating existing public and private
11 medical institutions into a cohesive statewide academic medical
12 system;
13 (e) Identification of strategies to expand programs for residency
14 training and postdoctoral fellowships for physicians with a focus on
15 specialties for which a high need exists and on underserved
16 geographic areas of this State;
17 (f) Exploration of opportunities for partnerships between the
18 public and private sector to support the operations of academic
19 medical centers and economic development relating to health care;
20 and
21 (g) An evaluation of the ability of various models of governance
22 for academic medical centers to ensure accountability, facilitate the
23 input of interested persons and entities and align the activities of the
24 academic medical center with the long-term goals of the State
25 Government relating to health care.
26 2. In conducting the study described in subsection 1, the
27 Patient Protection Commission shall consult with:
28 (a) Experts in health care, academic institutions and economics;
29 and
30 (b) Representatives of various communities in this State.
31 3. On or before November 6, 2026, the Patient Protection
32 Commission shall:
33 (a) Compile a comprehensive report of the findings and
34 recommendations resulting from the study conducted pursuant to
35 subsection 1; and
36 (b) Submit the report to:
37 (1) The Governor; and
38 (2) The Director of the Legislative Counsel Bureau for
39 transmittal to the next regular session of the Legislature.
40 4. As used in this section:
41 (a) “Academic medical center” means a medical school and its
42 affiliated teaching hospitals and clinics that:
43 (1) Operate a program for residency training and
44 postdoctoral fellowships for physicians, and

TEXT OF REPEALED SECTION
450B.215 Administrative sanctions for failure to comply
with requirements concerning electronic health information.
1. If the health authority receives notification from the
Department of Health and Human Services pursuant to NRS
439.5895 that the holder of a permit to operate an ambulance, air
ambulance or vehicle of a fire-fighting agency is not in compliance
with the requirements of subsection 4 of NRS 439.589, the health
authority may, after notice and the opportunity for a hearing in
accordance with the provisions of this chapter, require corrective
action or impose an administrative penalty in an amount established
by regulation of the board.
2. The health authority shall not suspend or revoke a permit for
failure to comply with the requirements of subsection 4 of
NRS 439.589.
